We had a similar experience to craig. We pulled in on Easter Sunday morning. The front parking was almost full.  My hubby a disabled veteren, pulled our truck up by the truck scales. He decided to stay in the running truck in case a semi needed to be weighed while i ran in to purchase the one item we needed . (Pretty unlikely on Easter Sunday, no trucks to be seen). As I approach the store a lady comes out trying to talk to me but doesn't speak much English but i figured out she was talking about where my hubby was parked.  I told her he will watch for a truck that is why he stayed in the running truck. I run to grab the one item, go to the counter and the guy tells me that now my hubby is blocking a portion of the scales and handicap parking. Mind u there are 2 handicap parking spots and the other one is open. We exchange a couple things back and forth about the situation and i can tell he is getting irritated that my hubby did not move immediately. Then he tells me that next time he will not serve us if he parks in a no parking zone.  All of this took less than 5 minutes and would have been quicker if they did not stop to chastise us.<//Review>

<rate>5<//rate>< text>
It was during the fires in late September, in the middle of the night we were evacuating.  We were heading out of town when we stopped to get gas, it was 1:30am and my daughter got a flat tire. Needless to say we didn't leave town that night, we slept on the floor at my husband's office.

The next morning I called Big O Tires, to inquire about tires.  We went back and forth with the options and how soon they could be delivered.  I was tired and exhausted, and stress needless to say. We had new tires on the car later that day and then we continued our evacuation.

During our evacuation I took a look at the tires and realized these were not the ones I wanted to purchase. When we came back into town, I went back to Big O and spoke with manger and the regional manager, they were both very understanding, they switched them out for the tires I had wanted.

Initially I thought the service person had made a mistake and ordered the wrong tires. But just yesterday, yes two months after the fire, I found my notes from my phone call with Big O and I saw that it was me who made the mistake!  I have to thank both managers for being compassionate as I hadn't slept much in days, I was trying to think of everything I needed to take care of in this evacuation mode.  These guys switched out my tires knowing I was the one who was mistaken.  I wanted to write this review to just let everyone know how caring the guys are at Big O.  I will forever be grateful.< /text>

< review>
I paid $100 for a front and rear gear oil change. I shopped around, used Groupon, and Blake and Matt were open to coming down on price, but it was by  far the best deal I could find. A smell associated with a disengaged clutch was gone afterwards. A few weeks later, I dropped my car off to diagnose a sound. They had it up for the better part of a day looking into it, but couldn't come up with a sure diagnosis, so they charged me nothing and told me to bring it to a transmission shop. It was great to get the honesty, and I was never pressed to come in for other miscellaneous work, even though this is a 2002 manual Impreza Outback with 2008 registration stickers that has the usual sitting-in-the-road-for-ten-years-not-getting-much-use kinks to work out (used purchase from family, trying to get an idea of how much it's worth).

Following up from yesterday: Transco diagnosed a transmission issue, as well. Transco, being the transmission shop, was able to delve more into the details, but I just wanted to repost that Big O was correct. Fix from Transco was quoted at $2k, which is about the car's value.< /review>

< Review>
This restaurant started from a food truck. Now it's found a permanent home in Pomona. Chef is taiwanese, food was mixture of asian influence, easy finger food that's gourmet. Was able to try top selling items for the last 8 years. Tasted lobster corndog, hamachi tartare taco. This was my favorite. All the sliders were great kobe beef slider, pork belly asian style slider. The meat melts in ur mouth. The fried oyster taco was interesting and different. Walnut shrimp taco was another favorite. They have spring rolls here too, will come back and try other breakfast and lunch items.</Review>

Very good place to eat. It's somewhat of asian & comfort food, mixed together. It's a very hip place to eat. Very well set up and located in downtown Pomona. You spend 10-$15 to eat, unless you get soup. Everything is picture perfect food when you receive it and the taste is very good. Also, the bread pudding is amazing!</review>

< text>
I purchased my car in August 2013 and took it down to get the windows tinted the 5%.  I was pleased with them.  The tint was super dark and with time I thought my eyes were adjusting to the darkness.  I added a sticker to the back of my window almost immediately and about a year and a half later decided I did not want the sticker on there anymore.  When I took the sticker off, it was dark where the sticker was and extremely light where the sticker wasn't.  The tint had faded dramatically.  I took my car back to them and their tinter said the tint they had used in the past was faulty and now they work with a better one.  I asked him if the tint was bad and he said yes, but now they add aluminum to the tint. I showed it to the co-owner and he said he would call me.  I called Super Tint a few days later and spoke to the co-owner and he said he would need to speak with his partner regarding what to do.  He let me know it might be a while since his business partner is in Spain.  I called back a few days later and he quoted me $75.  I told him I refuse to pay for another tint since they used faulty tint and it didn't even last a year.  He said he would get back to me.  I called him a few days later and he quoted me $50.  Again I told him absolutely not.  He said he would get back to me.  Again, a few days later I called him and he said $45.  I told him he must not understand, he sold me bad tint and now he expects me to pay to replace it.  This went on for several months and a different amount each time.  FINALLY he said he would do it for free.  Since August 6, 2016 I have been trying to get them to complete the work.  At one point the co-owner tried doing it and there were TONS of bubbles in it; he said he didn't have time to clean the windows from the previous tint.  Another time there was soapy water in my trunk (see picture); luckily I had Clawson Honda put a rubber lining in my trunk when I purchased it.  OF COURSE THE OWNER DENIED ANY RESPONSIBILITY!  I only noticed it when I went to Costco and was about to put my groceries in the trunk.  I have taken my car back to them at least 10 times and about 6 times to have the tint replaced since it is always scratched or has bubbles.  A couple of times I have brought my car in as scheduled to have it repaired to be informed at the end of the day, the tinters didn't come in since their cars are unreliable.  I am scheduled to go back in AGAIN on New Years EVE.  The co-owner TOLD me I need to go on Yelp and give Super Tint a good review, because they only take care of those that take care of them.  Seriously, was that a threat?? Sad when you can only get good reviews by threatening your customers!  If it is not done correctly this time, I will see them in court.  I am so DONE messing around with this!  Also, BEWARE the 5% tint is not as dark as advertised.< /text>

<gmap_id>0x80d95f1d3777e4f9:0xc30dca6d1f0fa9fc<//gmap_id><Resp>None<//Resp><Text>This is definitely one of my favorite places to explore nature. In addition to its natural beauty, it holds history, art, and environmental education opportunities. Typically less peopled than places like Mission Trails, this quiet little preserve is a great place for quiet reflection. It's trails vary from stroller friendly to hiker challenging (but I haven't come across anything crazy intense). There is some poison oak in sections of the park, but if you stay on the trails you can easily avoid it. The workers there are working hard to restore certain sections to their original native plants, so be sure to stay on the trails in any case. If you visit, be sure not to miss the mushroomed shaped hay bale house. On a hot day, it is a heavenly cool place to catch your breath, and the mosaic patio and sculptures outside it are truly charming.< /Text>< user_name>
Kathleen D< /user_name>

<user_id>113260988846405229857</user_id>< text>
Hidden gem of East County! If you are looking for a great place to hike you have to visit this place. There are a lot of trails. Some are not marked very well, but I am told they are in the process of working on that now. There is a beautiful Oak grove with a huge amount of Engelmann and Coast live oaks that provide a shady spot to walk and explore. There are lots of horseback riders and mountain bikers so don't be surprised if you need to share the trails. You can even bring your dog for a walk, but be sure to keep them on a leash at all times.<//text>

<time>1577644717835<//time><Rating>5</Rating>< username>
Jay Keyes</username>
< Text>
The specialty of Tito's La Especial are "tacos al vapor," aka steamed tacos. This delicious Mexican street food is also known as "tacos de canasta" (basket tacos) because they're traditionally layered in a big basket and sold by street vendors, many of whom hawk them from their bikes.

Tito's "Carne Deshebrada Taco Al Vapor" is excellent. Aside from steamed double corn tortillas comprising each taco's "shell," the chile-steeped shredded beef inside is soft, luscious, and as juicy as you'd want any meat to be. You do want to eat these quickly, before the tortillas begin to stick to the wrappers they are served in. Despite the fact they traditionally would be drizzled in oil (to help preserve them) and served out of a basket over the course of a day, these tacos are best made-to-order. I would also recommend the "Papas Taco Al Vapor," consisting of seasoned potatoes in a ranchera sauce, a loose mash of creamy crushed potatoes and firmer chunks, all colored orange from the sauce.

The "Taco Dorado de Carne Deshebrada" served here is the complete opposite of the al vapor tacos, as the tortilla is instead a crunchy deep-fried shell that is stuffed with stewed beef, lettuce, chopped tomatoes, and shredded cheese. Tito's does a decent job with this style of taco, but you really should stick to the al vapor tacos here, which are indeed "especial."

Tito's La Especial's salsa roja is made of fire and miracles and I recommend it be used on everything you eat here.</Text>
